4354     \textcolor{comment}{/* O.K., we were compiling our way through this definition and we've}
4355 \textcolor{comment}{       encountered the Dreaded and Dastardly Does.  Here's what we do}
4356 \textcolor{comment}{       about it.  The problem is that when we execute the word, we}
4357 \textcolor{comment}{       want to push its address on the stack and call the code for the}
4358 \textcolor{comment}{       DOES> clause by diverting the IP to that address.  But...how}
4359 \textcolor{comment}{       are we to know where the DOES> clause goes without adding a}
4360 \textcolor{comment}{       field to every word in the system just to remember it.  Recall}
4361 \textcolor{comment}{       that since this system is portable we can't cop-out through}
4362 \textcolor{comment}{       machine code.  Further, we can't compile something into the}
4363 \textcolor{comment}{       word because the defining code may have already allocated heap}
4364 \textcolor{comment}{       for the word's body.  Yukkkk.  Oh well, how about this?  Let's}
4365 \textcolor{comment}{       copy any and all heap allocated for the word down one stackitem}
4366 \textcolor{comment}{       and then jam the DOES> code address BEFORE the link field in}
4367 \textcolor{comment}{       the word we're defining.}
4368 \textcolor{comment}{}
4369 \textcolor{comment}{       Then, when (DOES>) (P\_dodoes) is called to execute the word, it}
4370 \textcolor{comment}{       will fetch that code address by backing up past the start of}
4371 \textcolor{comment}{       the word and seting IP to it.  Note that FORGET must recognise}
4372 \textcolor{comment}{       such words (by the presence of the pointer to P\_dodoes() in}
4373 \textcolor{comment}{       their wcode field, in case you're wondering), and make sure to}
4374 \textcolor{comment}{       deallocate the heap word containing the link when a}
4375 \textcolor{comment}{       DOES>-defined word is deleted.  */}
